Vietnamese Petition Delegates Depart Motherland Tomorrow Morning 170

▲Continued Submission of Four Supplementary Points to the Sino-French Commercial Treaty

▲Hope for National Unity Against External Forces

▲Industrial and Commercial Circles Urgently Study and Ensure Quality Products

Mr. Huang An and Mr. Xu Yixian, delegates of the Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Cochinchina, Vietnam, who came to the country to petition and seek the amendment of the Sino-French Commercial Treaty, entered Beijing last week. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has already agreed to negotiate with the French government within the shortest possible time. The delegates considered that the main objective had been achieved, so they returned to Shanghai to await the ship back to Vietnam. Yesterday, the delegates submitted four additional points to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. The original submission is excerpted as follows:

▲Supplementary Submission of Four Important Points: Submission for the supplementary submission of four points, requesting negotiations with France and prompt conclusion of the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty to safeguard the overseas Chinese in Vietnam, plus return to the country to petition and expedite the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty. During the time in Beijing, the esteemed Minister and Vice Minister of your Ministry (and various committee members) personally summoned and interviewed us and promised to negotiate with France within the shortest possible period to finalize and implement [the treaty], etc. The delegates, on behalf of more than 300,000 overseas Chinese in Vietnam, sincerely thank your esteemed Ministry (Commission). However, there are still four crucial facts regarding the amendment of this Commercial Treaty, which are supplemented below as a basis for negotiation: 1. Upon examining the Sino-French Commercial Treaty signed on May 16, 1930, Schedule A lists 27 categories of goods exported from our country to France that are subject to the lowest tariff rates, including wool, ham, leather, pork, raw silk, wax, musk, cattle horns, sweet potatoes, fresh fruit, marble, dried fruit or candied fruit, lead, black lead, lead ingots, pure tin, compound tin, tin ingots, ink and ink sticks, Chinese medicinal materials, lead with and without antimony, paper, cardboard, tanned leather fans. Very few other goods are shipped from our country to Vietnam; although they are nominally included, we do not actually benefit from them. The main goods that our country currently exports to Vietnam are silk fabrics (silk satins, damasks), tea, porcelain, sacrificial items (incense, candles, firecrackers, paper flowers, tin foil), food (noodles, rice flour, pastries, soy sauce), rattan and rattan products. These goods, which are the most frequently sold, are missing from the original list. The amendment of the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty must include these items. In the original list, except for retaining Chinese medicinal materials, brushes, paper, ink, fresh fruits, cooked fruits, cooked vegetables, tin items, and leather, the remaining items can be directly deleted. 2. In the Sino-French Commercial Treaty, although the original list only includes five categories of French goods shipped to China that are subject to the lowest tariff rates, namely coal, furs, woodenware, nutmeg, and rice, these items are practically beneficial. Among them, rice accounts for the largest share, followed by coal. Since rice is a staple food, there is a need to regulate shortages and surpluses. It should be studied whether special tax regulations can be included. 3. Appendix 3(a) of the Sino-French Commercial Treaty stipulates that France requires overseas Chinese in Vietnam to continue exercising their historically enjoyed special rights in relation to tax matters (i.e., surtaxes and other taxes). The special rights referred to by the French have now lost their special nature due to changes in circumstances, environment, personnel, and laws. Since rights have been extinguished, obligations should also be cancelled. Special attention should be paid to deleting this clause. 4. The amount of customs revenue is related to the prosperity of goods and population. The prosperity of import goods is related to the high or low customs tariff rates. Taking Chinese silk fabrics as an example, in the past, approximately 28 million taels were shipped from Shanghai to Vietnam each year. Since the increase in tariff rates, less than 2 million taels are shipped each year. The same applies to other goods. Therefore, the result of the increased tax rate in Vietnam is a loss for both sides. Furthermore, the hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese are an important factor in the rise and fall of Vietnamese industries. If the economic situation of the overseas Chinese falls into an absolutely depressed state, the Vietnamese government, although not necessarily facing complete ruin, will suffer mutual harm. This relationship of interests should be explained to France to encourage them to pay attention. The above four points are only the most obvious. In summary, the overseas Chinese in Vietnam are already in a very difficult situation. It is not enough to maintain their livelihoods unless the aforementioned points are reached, the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty is finalized, and prompt implementation is achieved. It is reasonable to resubmit four points to your esteemed Ministry (Commission) for review. It is sincerely requested that you promptly negotiate with France to conclude the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty, alleviate the suffering of the overseas Chinese, and ensure public convenience. In addition to submitting separately, we respectfully submit this.

▲The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Approval Order to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce: Regarding the submission prepared by Huang and Xu when the two delegates entered Beijing, requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to promptly negotiate with the French government, the association received an approval order from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday, stating, "Received and noted. The Sino-French Vietnam Treaty is yet to be approved and implemented due to the unfinished schedule. The schedule is currently being actively negotiated by the Ministry with the French side. Once completed and finalized, the treaty can be approved and implemented by both parties. Please be informed accordingly." The association has forwarded the approval to Huang and Xu for their information.

▲Departing Shanghai for Vietnam Tomorrow Morning: According to Mr. Huang and Mr. Xu from the Vietnamese overseas Chinese delegation speaking to the National News Agency yesterday, they were greatly grateful that their petition for the Vietnamese overseas Chinese had been kindly received by the government and various organizations, who had generously accommodated their opinions and sincerely provided guidance and assistance. Now that their mission is completed, they are scheduled to board the French mail ship tomorrow morning to bid farewell to the motherland and return to Vietnam. Upon arrival, in addition to striving to promote patriotism among the overseas Chinese, they hope that the country will unite and work together to face external forces. Industrial and commercial circles, in addition to urgently seeking to improve product quality, must further develop foreign trade. This is the sincere prayer of overseas Chinese living under the eaves of others, they said. The French mail ship *Général Metzinger*, which Mr. Huang and others will be traveling on, left Shanghai yesterday morning. The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and other organizations will send representatives to board the ship with the two delegates tonight.

Details of the Sinking of the Fuqing 171

▲Arson for Help Was Not Due to Carelessness

▲Distressed Crew and Passengers Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

▲Cargo Loss Exceeds 300,000

The sinking of the Fuqing steamer of the Qipu Fuxing Public Company in the outer Dongsha area of Wusong has been reported in yesterday's newspaper. Further details of the incident are reported as follows:

▲Boiler Damaged En Route: The Fuqing ship specializes in the Shanghai-Quanzhou route. On the 16th of this month, it set sail from Shanghai fully loaded with cargo for Quanzhou. Around 11:00 AM, after departing, around 4:00 PM, it reached the outer Dongsha waters of Wusong. The boiler suddenly broke down. The old engineer reported to the captain, who then ordered the ship to drop anchor and stop sailing to repair the boiler. Repairing the boiler took from 4:00 PM to 7:40 PM, but it was not yet completed and still could not sail. The crew members, except for those working, went to their cabins to sleep. At 7:50 PM, the ship suddenly tilted to the right and very quickly. Within a few minutes, the ship was lying horizontally on the sea. The cargo on deck all fell into the sea, and the items in the cabins were tossed to one side. The passengers in bed also fell down.

▲Calling for Help in the Dark Without Response: After the ship tilted, seawater rushed into the cabins wildly, and the furnaces in the engine room were submerged in water. The whole ship lost power. Passengers and crew members struggled out of their cabins in the dark. Unable to walk, they climbed onto the railing of the port side deck barefoot and disheveled. Due to the suddenness of the escape, many crew members and passengers did not have time to put on clothes. At that time, the whistle could not be sounded, and flags could not be hoisted in the dark. The ship was sinking rapidly. All the crew members could only shout for help. Although a ship was seen passing by, it was too far away, and their calls went unanswered.

▲Starting a Fire to Signal for Rescue: By 9:30 PM, seeing that the ship was about to sink and all dozens of people were about to be buried at sea, the crew members and the captain finally decided to set fire to signal for rescue, hoping that another ship would see them. However, there was no way to retrieve the flares, so they found a way to move the firewood carried in the cabin to the riverside platform and set it on fire. The firewood was ignited very quickly, and the fire lit up the sky in an instant. At that time, the Ruikang of the Sanfa Company and the Zhengzhou of the Hezhong Company were coming to Shanghai from Qingdao and Haizhou, respectively. Seeing the large fire on the sea, they suspected that it was due to a merchant ship's carelessness and came to the rescue.

▲Entire Crew and Passengers Rescued: The Ruikang was the first to see the fire. The comprador Xiaojueren ordered the ship to speed towards Dongsha. Approaching the Fuqing, they saw that the ship had capsized and sunk, and the crew members, sailors, and passengers were clinging to the deck railing, their lower bodies already submerged in the water. In the urgent situation, the Ruikang immediately launched a large sampan to rescue people. After three trips, they rescued the captain Bai Ximan (Russian), driver Le Dagen, old engineer Liu Fuquan, second engineer Jin, supervisor Lin Liulian, and water passengers, a total of more than 40 people. The Zhengzhou also arrived and sent a sampan to rescue a total of 15 passengers and sailors. The rescued crew and passengers were soaked, and their luggage was not retrieved. After boarding the ship, the crew members of the two ships took good care of them, helping them dry their wet clothes. Around 7:00 AM yesterday, they were transported to Shanghai and disembarked at the Hongxing Wharf.

▲Five More Sailors Arrived Later: There were two stokers, a servant, an oiler, and a waiter who had boarded a small sampan and left the Fuqing when the accident occurred. By yesterday afternoon, they had not been found, and everyone suspected that they must have met with an accident. Just as they were anxiously hoping for news, the five men reported at 3:30 PM that they had arrived safely in Shanghai. After the Ruikang rescued the crew members, the Fuqing sank within half an hour. According to the distressed passengers speaking to reporters yesterday, if the Ruikang had arrived an hour later, the entire ship would have been lost to the sea.

▲Estimated Cargo Loss: The Fuqing was loaded with 14,000 bags of flour and bran, more than 2,000 pieces of groceries and oil drums, pears, etc., all of which were lost. The total loss of cargo is estimated at 200,000 yuan. The ship was purchased by Fuxing in 1924 and was originally a patrol vessel of the Datong Telegraph Bureau. The iron plates were quite thick, and the ship was solid. The declared tonnage was 950 tons. This sinking will cause a loss of 100,000 yuan for the ship itself. In addition, the clothing and luggage of the crew members and passengers will also require more than 10,000 yuan. The ship was originally insured for 50,000 taels for marine insurance. It was suddenly withdrawn this year, insuring only 30,000 taels. The cargo owners and insurance companies have been notified yesterday.

▲Personnel Dispatched for Inspection Today: The accident of this ship is indeed peculiar. Anchoring and capsizing is unheard of. After repeated investigations by reporters with the victims, it was said that the cargo was overloaded on the deck, and the decks were covered with heavy oil drums, so the top was heavy and the bottom was light, causing it to tilt to one side and causing the disaster. However, the company still needs to investigate the truth of the accident. It has been agreed to send a small motorboat with the shipowners to the scene of the accident to investigate this morning. When the Ruikang came to Shanghai yesterday morning, the Fuqing was only one foot above the surface of the water. At high tide, it is feared that it will sink completely.

Residents in Pengpu District Automatically Remove Forest Stumps Placed to Encircle Land 172

▲Railway Bureau Reports and Requests Instructions Separately Upon Receiving News

▲Villagers in the District Petition Party Headquarters Again

The villagers of Wangjiajing, Zhuxiang, and Zhao Jiahuayuan in Pengpu District, because their petition to the Municipal Government had not yielded results, convened a meeting on their own initiative. Each village was responsible for removing all the land enclosure stumps, forests, and notices near their village to show their determination. This morning, more than 700 villagers implemented the plan and removed the stumps, throwing them into the river. The notices posted at the Wangjiajing Zhuang entrance of the Jiaotong Road were also thrown into the river. When a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency inspected the area yesterday, all the wooden stumps erected by the Ministry of Railways were gone, and the boundaries could no longer be distinguished.

▲Railway Bureau Reports: After receiving the news, the two railway bureaus immediately notified the Municipal Government to order the Public Security and Land Bureaus to protect the area and reported to the Ministry of Railways and requested instructions on how to handle the situation.

▲Villagers' Statement: According to the villagers, after the stumps were removed, if the Ministry of Railways sent personnel to the village to measure and re-erect the stumps before allowing detours, the villagers were prepared to reject the measurement.

▲Petition to Party Headquarters: The villagers' representatives, Hou Xuanqing, and others, led more than 400 villagers to the Municipal Party Headquarters again at 4:00 PM yesterday, holding white petition flags. However, because the office hours were over and no one was in charge, the petition did not yield results, and they left.

Pan Yunchao Discusses the Current Situation of the Northeastern Volunteer Army 173

▲Able to Settle Down When the Green Gauze Curtain Falls

▲Singing Uninterrupted Amidst the Sound of Gunfire

▲Lack No Sharp Weapons but Lack Supplies

Mr. Pan Yunchao, a member of the Central Committee, recently went to the Central Government to negotiate the issue of assisting the Volunteer Army. Now that the matter is completed, Mr. Pan returned to Shanghai yesterday and reported on the recent activities of the Northeastern Volunteer Army. They are recorded below.

▲Time of Panic: According to Mr. Pan, the Volunteer Army's ability to operate in the Northeast during the summer and autumn months, causing pain to the Japanese army and exhausting them, relied entirely on the dense green gauze curtain of sorghum. The fertile fields stretched for thousands of miles, and the Volunteer Army relied on this natural barrier to advance to attack and retreat to defend. The heroic feats of the past few months have been witnessed by the world. However, at this time, early winter has arrived, and the sorghum has withered and fallen. The green gauze curtain, which was regarded as the only natural barrier, has disappeared with the seasons. Therefore, the people are deeply worried that with the loss of the natural barrier, the Volunteer Army will have nowhere to stand and will lose the opportunity to launch attacks.

▲Peacefully Passed: Contrary to what we deeply worried about, the Northeastern Volunteer Army authorities knew that they would have nowhere to stand with the loss of this natural barrier. Therefore, they had long utilized the towering mountains as a base for retreat and concealment. The mountains in the Northeast are continuous, the trees provide shade, and the terrain is dangerous, which the Japanese army deeply fears. The area within these mountains is quite vast, not only capable of accommodating tens of thousands of Volunteer Army soldiers but also extremely prosperous with villages and residences. The Volunteer Army used this as a base to defend it firmly. When the Japanese army came to encircle, they hid deeply and did not come out. When the Japanese army was lax, they waited for the opportunity to attack. Even if the Japanese army did not avoid hardship and led troops to advance sharply, they could still design to annihilate them. Therefore, the Japanese army never dared to go deep.

Singing Uninterrupted: The Volunteer Army's supplies and other necessities are extremely difficult in these deep mountains surrounded by enemies. However, because these towering mountains have many residents, the food issue can still be dealt with. Furthermore, since people each have the determination to die, both the Volunteer Army and the residents, men and women, old and young, can cooperate wholeheartedly. They know that once the Volunteer Army is defeated and the Japanese army moves in, both the good and the bad will be destroyed under the Japanese army's oppressive force. However, the Japanese army often sends aircraft to bomb them. But because the trees are lush all day long, making it difficult to find targets, the destructive power is minimal. The people have also become accustomed to this and do not find it frightening. Recently, it was reported that in the Volunteer Army base in the deep mountains of Liaonan and Liaodong, the original elementary and middle schools are still able to teach as usual, and the sound of reading is uninterrupted. This is also something we never imagined.

Self-Made Sharp Weapons: In addition, there is another thing that we never imagined: This group of soldiers, retreating and hiding in the deep mountains, is now being surrounded by the Japanese army. Although the Japanese army does not dare to go deep, they have to mobilize troops to encircle them, and their only goal is to cut off the Volunteer Army's supplies of ammunition and other necessities to weaken their combat capability. Unexpectedly, recent reports indicate that there are many outstanding talents in the Kangbei Volunteer Army who can come up with solutions in the absence of solutions and self-make sharp weapons. All gunpowder, bullets, hand grenades, rifles, and even artillery can be self-made. Therefore, this group of Volunteer Army soldiers hiding in the mountains and being surrounded has a small arsenal with this new invention, and they are not feeling the difficulty. The Japanese army authorities are also extremely surprised by this and cannot figure it out no matter how hard they try.

Exhausted: Although many Northeastern Volunteer Army troops are surrounded by the Japanese army in the deep mountains, most of them can still carry out fully mobile strategic warfare in the snowy and icy conditions because the Japanese army's troops cannot reach them. They often take advantage of high winds and dark nights to carry out raids on camps. They may have thousands of people, or as few as two or three people, using feigned attacks or outwitting the enemy. Every time they raid the camp late at night, the Volunteer Army only fires one shot, and the Japanese army, hearing this alarm, does not know how many troops are outside. They then collapse and fire bullets indiscriminately, wasting ammunition in vain. The Volunteer Army has already left at this time. This action is enough to make the Japanese army both shocked and afraid. Mobilizing troops and generals has become increasingly exhausting, and the Volunteer Army has already taken advantage of the weakness of their troops to attack.

Difficulty in Supply: The Volunteer Army's combat capability has been clearly determined and has not been reduced due to the destruction of the green gauze curtain. The Japanese army's claim that it could clear the area within three months has also been found to be unreliable. However, what they feel most difficult is the lack of clothing. To this day, most of the Volunteer Army soldiers still lack winter clothing. Therefore, compatriots at home and abroad should find ways to help them so that the Volunteer Army can survive this winter and be able to defeat the Japanese army to the death next spring. In addition, it is now known that fire has disappeared from the Volunteer Army's location, and they have restored the old method of finding fire from decades ago. And kerosene and other items have had to be replaced with soybean oil, peanut oil, etc.

Unified Command: Furthermore, the Volunteer Army's combat effectiveness is sufficient to exhaust the Japanese army. However, due to the lack of unified command, even large-scale plans often cannot be realized. Therefore, it has been suggested that a military commission be established to be responsible for directing operations. In addition, this organization can also fairly distribute the Volunteer Army's supplies, finances, and supervision, ensuring that there is no imbalance. In this way, military power can be unified, and there is no need to worry about supplies. In the future, it will be easier to fight in the Northeast. Also, now that the Japanese army knows that it cannot deal with the Northeastern Volunteer Army, it often buys local militias for its use. This is a very painful thing.

Three Million Yuan

Regarding the collection and transportation of cash in Shanghai for the Northeast, two batches have already been exported, totaling more than 5.2 million yuan. The Second Batch of the Volunteer Army Medical Relief Team Departs Today 175

The first batch of the Northeast Volunteer Army Medical Relief Team departed from Beiping on the 15th of last month to Kailu, providing medical relief under He Qingming's department under Feng Zhanhai. The second batch of team members underwent physical examinations and reviews of their medical knowledge yesterday. The team also judged their will and character, and it has been decided that they will depart today. Details are recorded below.

Screening of Departing Team Members: Starting at 8:00 AM yesterday, the team conducted physical examinations of the team members at the Nanyang Hospital on Huangjia Road, assessing the team members' character and qualifications. After arriving at the hospital, team members first reported at the registration desk, then went to the examination room. Examiners Huang Zhong, Wang Mengying, and Huangfu Jun, among others, were responsible for the examinations. They also asked questions about general medical and rescue knowledge such as:

What types of wounds are there? What are the first aid treatments for wounds? What are the methods of wound disinfection? How many types of disinfectants are there? What are the pre-operative disinfection procedures (surgical treatments, etc.)? After the examination, forms were filled out. The teams then went to the screening room, where screeners Fei Jian, Tao Zuyin, and Wang Changyan, among others, assessed will, character, qualifications, and history. During the screening, they inquired about various rescue skills to assess the team member's character and the like. These were also recorded on forms for future reference. Yesterday, over 80 team members were examined and screened. The examination and screening will continue today.

Departure This Afternoon: After the examination and screening are completed today, some team members will be selected as the second batch of departing team members, totaling over 20 people. The remaining team members will depart in the third batch. At 11:00 PM this afternoon, the team, led by team leader Fei Jian, will depart on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway night express, first to Bengbu. There, they will gather with the 80+ members of the team’s second company. Then, Fei Jian and the second company commander Chen Ruchen will go to Beiping to negotiate locations, winter clothing and food, and other issues. Once the negotiations are completed, they will lead the second batch of team members out of the pass, directly to the battlefield, without delay. After the second batch arrives at the battlefield, commander Chen Ruchen of the second company will be responsible for everything at the front. Team leader Fei Jian will return to Shanghai to plan for the departure of the third batch of team members. According to team leader Fei Jian yesterday, the team is currently planning to send 20 batches, each with about 100 people. The team’s existence is equal to that of the Northeast's Volunteer Army: once the Volunteer Army is dissolved, the team will also come to an end. If the Volunteer Army exists for one day, the seventh team will continue its efforts and rescue for one day, vowing not to withdraw halfway.

Submitting a Report to the Party Headquarters for Guidance: To facilitate the team's operations and for the sake of prudence, the team will gradually establish a board of directors, a board of supervisors, etc. Yesterday, a special report was submitted to the municipal party headquarters, requesting that personnel be dispatched for guidance. The original report stated: "Regarding the report, since the establishment of our team, patriotic compatriots at home and abroad have given enthusiastic support. The various developments have been reported one after another. The first batch of team members above Beiping departed for the war zone on the deleted date of last month to carry out medical relief work. The second batch is now organized and ready to depart soon, and the third batch is also in active progress. Now that the team's affairs are increasing, the original eight members are insufficient to handle them. In addition, the community donations are increasing daily. For the sake of prudence, the team intends to organize a board of directors to handle all affairs and a board of supervisors to supervise them. The board of directors will hire bankers, business leaders, lawyers, accountants, doctors, and enthusiastic patriotic philanthropists with experience to organize design and finance committees to guide and handle matters. Attached is a draft of the board of directors' organization, submitting it for your review. If it is appropriate, we request that you approve it and dispatch personnel to supervise and guide us, so that we may follow and benefit the rescue efforts. This is for the public good. Respectfully submitted to the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters."

Donations Received Yesterday: Yichangxing, Yuxinxiang, one yuan each. Nanrenhe, Beirenhe, five yuan each. Wanyuxiang, two yuan. Dafeng, Wanli, Fuhexiang, Weida, Yu Zhangyuan, Xiecheng, Asia, Medali, Anonymous, one yuan each. Henglong, Ren Yunsheng, Zhongyang, Tongrenhe, Tongyu, Wansheng, Guohua, Jixiangyong, Tongyichun, 50 cents each. Yesterday, the employees of Hongzhang Textile Washing and Dyeing Factory donated 294 comforters to the team.

The Entire Illegal Loan Contract for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Signed by Li Guojie 176

▲Officially Announced by the Ministry of Communications the Night Before Last

Divided into 1) Contract, 2) Memorandum, 3) Lease, 4) Contract for Payment of Mortgage Money

According to the Central News Agency, the much-publicized illegal loan contracted by Li Guojie of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) with the American China Ventures, Inc., the Ministry of Communications, after repeated research and review of the original contract, believed that the contract was extremely detrimental to the interests of the CMSNC. The case has been severely handled by the Central Political Council and the Executive Yuan according to law, with the aim of revoking the harmful contract. In order to clarify the content and Li Guojie's mistakes to the people, the Ministry of Communications publicly announced the entire illegal contract on the night of the 16th. This contract is divided into: 1) Contract, containing 19 articles; 2) Contract Memorandum, divided into parts A and B, and 15 sections of methods; 3) Lease, divided into 15 articles; and 4) Contract specifying the payment dates and amounts of the mortgage money, divided into 17 articles, totaling four major parts. A copy of the entire contract has now been found and is disclosed below.

Contract: China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (hereinafter referred to as the CMSNC; this abbreviation, along with successors, heirs, or representatives, is included), American China Ventures, Inc. (hereinafter referred to as the Ventures; this abbreviation, along with successors or heirs, is included),

For the purpose of both parties signing an mortgage not exceeding Shanghai Tael 10 million on September 5, 1932, and with the CMSNC specially authorized by the Ventures to issue bonds for the aforementioned mortgage, the regulations regarding the payment date and amount of the mortgage are fully stated in this contract. Having been agreed upon by both parties, the articles are stipulated as follows:

(1) The CMSNC is willing to hand over to the Ventures the real estate specified in the mortgage agreement signed with the Ventures on September 5, 1932, including Land Register Nos. 54A, 54B, 53, and 53A in the Central District of the Shanghai International Settlement, as well as the existing buildings on the land and any new buildings constructed during the mortgage period, as collateral for the bonds issued as stated in this contract. (It is verified that the aforementioned real estate belongs to the property of the CMSNC's Accumulated Property Co., Ltd., which has fully approved the mortgage and the matters stated in this contract. The board of directors of the company has acknowledged it, and the chairman of the board will sign and seal the contract and mortgage agreement as proof.) (2) Mutually acknowledged by both parties, for the purpose of raising the aforementioned mortgage money, the Ventures may, using the aforementioned property listed in the mortgage agreement as collateral, issue bonds with a total face value not exceeding Shanghai Tael 10 million, with a term of 20 years, at a net receipt of 85%. Furthermore, the issued bonds shall be completely separate from the bonds already issued or to be issued by the Ventures or its designee in order to be recognized. (3) Mutually agreed by both parties that the CMSNC shall pay the Ventures interest on the mortgage at an annual rate of 9%, calculated based on the face value of the issued bonds. The interest shall be paid every three months, and any interest not paid on time shall also accrue compound interest at an annual rate of 9%. (4) Mutually acknowledged and agreed by both parties that the amount of discount and interest on the mortgage loan and bond issuance, whether profit or loss, is the sole responsibility of the Ventures and has nothing to do with the CMSNC. (5) After this contract and the mortgage agreement mentioned in this contract have been formally signed and sealed by both parties, the Ventures shall, in accordance with the actual receipt discount and all the regulations stated in this contract, immediately issue the first batch of bonds for this mortgage loan, with a face value of Shanghai Tael 4 million, to meet the CMSNC's needs as follows: (A) Repay the loan of one million taels previously mortgaged to Citibank with Land Register Nos. 54A, 54B, and 53 of the British Municipal Council, and the interest due. (B) Repay the loan of 470,000 taels previously mortgaged to the China Ventures, Inc. with Land Register No. 53A, and the interest due. (C) Pay the CMSNC 500,000 taels to meet the CMSNC's business needs. (D) Allocate funds for the construction of the most modern office building at the corner of Szechuan Road and Fuzhou Road as originally decided. (E) Pay the Ventures 2.5% of the face value of the first batch of bonds issued for this mortgage. (6) The remaining amount of the bonds with a face value of Shanghai Tael 10 million shall be issued by the Ventures in successive periods at appropriate times, and the proceeds shall be used primarily for the construction of the newest office building on the aforementioned land specified in the mortgage agreement. (7) Both parties acknowledge that all matters related to building construction shall be under the full management of the Ventures. The plans and specifications for the new buildings on the land specified in this contract and the mortgage agreement shall be submitted by the Ventures to the CMSNC for record. It is also expressly acknowledged by both parties that all technical issues regarding the style and engineering of the buildings shall be solely managed by the Ventures. (8) During the mortgage period, the CMSNC acknowledges and agrees to pay the Ventures a rental commission of 5% based on the amount of rent collected by the Ventures on its behalf. All management and services for the buildings shall also be borne by the Ventures. (9) Regarding the cash proceeds from the sale of bonds, from the date of receipt to the date of the next payment to the CMSNC, interest shall be calculated at the bank's current account interest rate. (10) The CMSNC also acknowledges that from the date of sale of the bonds stipulated in this contract, all rents on the real estate mentioned in this contract, and all rents currently collected by the Ventures, and whose real estate belongs to the CMSNC and is not within the scope of this contract, and which have already been mortgaged by the CMSNC to the Ventures and are not within the scope of this contract, and future rent, etc. (attached rent bill) shall be collected by the Ventures. This income shall first be used to pay the interest on other mortgages due to the Ventures, and then to pay the interest on this mortgage stipulated under this contract. If the collected interest is insufficient to pay the interest on this mortgage stipulated under this contract, the unpaid interest shall be added to the CMSNC's debt account as an outstanding interest account, which shall also accrue compound interest at an annual rate of 9%. If there are sufficient funds from the collected rent or other sources, it shall be paid off immediately. If there are any surplus funds from the collected rent, they shall be immediately deposited into the CMSNC's bond repayment reserve fund account for the purpose of paying the total face value of the bonds issued for this mortgage under this contract and the interest due on this mortgage. The Ventures shall make every effort to ensure that the funds in this income reserve fund account are used to generate the maximum possible interest. The maximum interest obtained must also be deposited into the bond repayment reserve fund account. The amount already deposited into the CMSNC's bond repayment reserve fund account shall be managed by the Ventures in full, but if the CMSNC has a good plan to generate higher interest on this reserve fund, it may make suggestions to the Ventures. (11) The CMSNC acknowledges that when occupying newly built buildings, it is willing to pay the corresponding rent, but it will not pay rent for the currently occupied old buildings. The CMSNC also acknowledges that if the location of the old buildings currently occupied by the CMSNC is needed for new construction, upon notification from the Ventures, it shall move out within three months from the date of the notification. (12) The CMSNC acknowledges that it shall pay the Ventures 2.5% of the face value of the bonds issued under this contract. This payment shall be paid on the date of sale of each bond. (13) The Ventures agrees that the various income and expenditure accounts under this contract shall be completely independent and separate from the Ventures' inherent business accounts. (14) The CMSNC acknowledges and agrees that no part of the real estate mentioned in this contract shall be re-mortgaged externally, and guarantees responsibility for handling all negotiations to eliminate any legal interference. Furthermore, any negotiations regarding existing second mortgages on the property shall be the responsibility of the CMSNC and have nothing to do with the Ventures. (15) Both parties understand and agree that in the event that the CMSNC wishes to sell all or part of the aforementioned real estate during the term of this contract or before this mortgage has been cleared, the Ventures shall have the right of first refusal to purchase all or part of the property. It is also agreed by both parties that whether the sale is handled by the CMSNC or the Ventures, a standard commission of 2.5% shall be paid to the Ventures. (16) In the event that the CMSNC is unable to pay the principal and interest due on the aforementioned mortgage represented by the total face value of the issued bonds, or the funds in the CMSNC's bond repayment reserve fund account are insufficient to pay all or part of the principal due on the aforementioned mortgage represented by the total face value of the issued bonds, and the interest due on this mortgage, the Ventures shall have full power to dispose of the property, either by public auction or by private sale, of all or part of the properties mentioned in this contract to repay the principal and interest due. If this is still insufficient, the CMSNC shall compensate in other ways. If there is a surplus, the Ventures shall pay it to the CMSNC after clearing the principal and interest due. (17) The Ventures acknowledges that once the principal, other payments, and commissions, etc., of the bonds issued under this contract have been fully paid, all the real estate mentioned in this contract shall be transferred back to the CMSNC by the Ventures. (18) Both parties mutually acknowledge that from the date of signing the contract, regardless of any problems, disputes, or disagreements that may arise, they shall immediately engage two impartial persons. One impartial person shall be selected by the CMSNC, and one shall be selected by the Ventures. If the two impartial persons cannot agree, the two impartial persons shall jointly elect a leading impartial person, all of whom shall be determined in accordance with current American law. The result of the determination, whether determined by the two impartial persons or by the leading impartial person, shall be acknowledged and obeyed by both parties, and they are willing to comply with it. If one party has notified the other party of its appointed impartial person and the other party fails to designate or refuses to designate its impartial person within ten days, then regardless of any problems, disputes, or disagreements, the party that has already selected an impartial person may immediately submit it to that party's impartial person for sole decision. It is also acknowledged and agreed by both parties that in all of the above situations, the result of the determination of the impartial person appointed by the one party shall be fully obeyed by that party and the other party, and the impartial person of the one party shall be regarded as being appointed by both parties. (19) This contract is a part of this mortgage agreement and is an attachment to this mortgage agreement. Contract established on September 5, 1932. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, President of the Board of Directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Witness, General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Witness, Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Accumulated Property Co., Ltd., Witness, American China Ventures, Inc., Witness. All of the above have been approved by the Supervisory Office of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company of the Ministry of Communications of the National Government. Seal of the Supervisory Office of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company of the Ministry of Communications. (This is a translation; the original is in English.)

Memorandum to the Contract: China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (hereinafter referred to as Party A; this abbreviation, along with successors, heirs, or representatives, is included), American China Ventures, Inc. (hereinafter referred to as Party B; this abbreviation, along with successors, heirs, or representatives, is included). Now, Party A's existing merchant ships are too old and uneconomical, and it wishes to purchase a considerable number of ships to replace them. Party A and Party B have consulted with the American Dollar Steamship Lines. The points agreed upon by both parties are recorded below. (A) Dollar Steamship Lines is willing to purchase suitable ships for Party A at the lowest price, up to 30 ships, for Party A's current Yangtze River and North and South Seas shipping business. (B) For the mutual benefit of Party A and Dollar Steamship Lines, Party A and Dollar Steamship Lines shall establish a mutual cooperation agreement in the shipping business. The most important of these is that the two companies shall mutually issue through bills of lading, so that the goods transported by the two companies can be directly transported from their respective export locations to the destination. Therefore, Dollar Steamship Lines' responsibility for purchasing ships on behalf of the CMSNC, and its willingness to undertake such purchases, were mutually acknowledged and agreed upon on December 11 of last year in Shanghai by Li Weihou, the chairman of the board of directors representing the CMSNC, Guo Waifeng, the commissioner for reorganizing the CMSNC representing the National Government of Nanjing, Dollar Staley, the vice president of Dollar Steamship Lines, Steiger, the Shanghai manager of Dollar Steamship Lines, and Detry, the president of Party B. As the general office of Dollar Steamship Lines is located in San Francisco, California, USA, and the Shanghai manager of Dollar Steamship Lines is currently in the United States, and as the proposed matter is of great importance, all detailed terms must be discussed and stipulated again by Party A and Dollar Steamship Lines before a final mutual agreement can be reached. Therefore, Party A and Party B deem it appropriate to first sign a preliminary contract, including important principles, as the basis for the final contract. This contract is based on the receipt by Party B of one silver dollar from Party A, and Party B is willing to first stipulate the important terms with Party A on behalf of Dollar Steamship Lines. After this stipulation, Dollar Steamship Lines shall purchase the agreed number of ships for Party A from its general offices and branch offices in Europe and the Americas. It is also agreed by both parties to handle the matter separately in accordance with the following sections: (1) Investigate where there are ships that can be purchased and are suitable for Party A's shipping needs. (2) Before purchasing all ships, the detailed condition, drawings, age, and lowest purchase price of the ship shall be sent to Party A for review. (3) All ships that have been reviewed and approved by Party A in accordance with Article 2 shall be purchased by Dollar Steamship Lines on behalf of the CMSNC, and the cost shall be recorded in Party A's debt account. (4) The actual price paid and all expenses incurred, including the expenses for each ship to sail to Shanghai or other ports in China for delivery, shall be verified and calculated separately. (5) All ship purchase contracts and related account documents shall be sent to Party A for verification and storage. (6) Party A shall pay Dollar Steamship Lines a commission of 1.25% based on the actual price of each ship as remuneration for the company's purchase of each ship on behalf of the company and for transporting the ship to China. (7) Before Party A has paid all the actual price, all expenses, and the 1.25% commission in full, Party A shall pay interest at the normal rate of 9% until the date of full payment. This interest shall be paid on the third month from the date of interest accrual. If the interest is not paid on time, compound interest shall be calculated at an annual rate of 9%. (8) Before Party A has paid the full price of the ships, the ownership of each ship shall belong to Dollar Steamship Lines, and each ship shall be supervised by Dollar Steamship Lines. (9) Dollar Steamship Lines shall send the detailed accounts of all expenses for each ship under its supervision, along with receipts, to Party A for verification and storage on a regular basis. (10) During the period of Dollar Steamship Lines' supervision of each ship, Party A shall have the right to use the ships separately for all commercial shipping purposes. (11) Before the price of the ship has been paid in full, each ship shall be registered in the United States and fly the American flag, but all national government restrictions on foreign merchants' merchant ships along the rivers and seas in foreign countries shall be waived. (12) All net income from each ship's business, excluding all expenses due to Party A, shall be paid to Dollar Steamship Lines in order to repay the price of the ship. (13) All income and payments related to each ship supplied under this contract shall be recorded separately in the account of each ship. These accounts shall be managed by qualified personnel, and these qualified personnel shall be recommended by Party B or Dollar Steamship Lines. (14) In order to increase the security of Party B and Dollar Steamship Lines, Party A is willing to submit all deeds or Chinese deeds of the wharves and real estate in various ports that have been mortgaged to HSBC to Party B or Dollar Steamship Lines for storage as additional collateral for the ship prices, expenses, and commissions paid by Party B on behalf of Party A. Memorandum to the Contract established on September 6, 1932. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, President of the Board of Directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Witness, General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Witness, American China Ventures, Inc., Witness. All of the above have been approved by the Supervisory Office of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company of the Ministry of Communications of the National Government. The Ministry of Finance Will Allocate Funds to Recover China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Shares 177

The Property Affairs Department has dispatched Cai Lisheng to take over.

Yesterday, the Ministry of Transportation announced the contract between the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's General Manager, Li Guojie, and Supervisor Chen Fumu, who were detained, and the American-owned China Trading Company to clarify the truth to the public. As for the recovery of state-owned shares, each set is valued at fifty taels. A share registration method has been drafted and ordered to be handled by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Board of Directors. The registration method is recorded as follows:

Share Registration Method (Beijing Telegraph): After the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is nationalized, the Ministry of Transportation will return commercial shares and has specifically formulated the following share registration methods: (1) Share registration for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will be handled at the company's offices in Nanjing, Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou, Guangzhou, and Hong Kong. (2) All owners or pledgees of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company shares should, within the period specified in Article 3, submit their shares to the designated China Merchants Steam Navigation Company for verification, fill out a registration application form according to the prescribed format, and apply for registration. If someone is entrusted to apply on their behalf, a letter of entrustment should also be attached. (3) The registration period is from December 1, 1932, to February 28, 1933. Those who fail to apply for registration within the deadline will have their shares invalidated. (4) A shareholder or pledgee must hold a full set of shares, as traditionally recognized by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which is two navigation shares and one property share, to apply for registration. Those holding less than a full set of shares may combine with others to apply for registration. (5) The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company should provide receipts to applicants for the shares they submit for verification and record the applicant's name and receipt number on the back of the shares. The format of the receipt will be determined separately. (6) After the registration period expires, the Shanghai General Bureau of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will collect the application forms and shares from all locations, compare them with the share stubs, and conduct a detailed review. Those deemed authentic will have the "China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Verified" stamp affixed to the back of the shares and will be submitted to the Ministry of Transportation for announcement. The receipt number will be the same as in Article 7. The method of payment will be determined separately. (7) The price of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company shares will be 50 taels of silver per set, according to the National Government's order. (8) China Merchants Steam Navigation Company shares cannot be transferred or registered under a new name after registration begins.

The Ministry of Finance has Raised Funds (Beijing Telegraph): According to information from the Ministry of Transportation, the total face value of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company shares is approximately 12 million, equivalent to 440 million. At 50 taels per set, a total of 2.2 million taels of cash is required. The Ministry of Finance has already raised the necessary funds and will issue payments according to value after the registration procedures are completed.

A Record of Gao Tingzi's Remarks (Beijing Telegraph): Gao Tingzi, Director of the Navigation Administration Department of the Ministry of Transportation, stated that the four types of property mortgage contracts of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company involve a significant loss of navigation sovereignty. The government will definitely not recognize them, and they are purely the assertions of Li Guojie and others, and are naturally invalid according to the law. Although American merchants are unwilling to give up their vested rights, the Ministry of Transportation, in order to protect national rights, will first recover the four wharf properties and then negotiate with them based on reason. Chen Fumu and Li Guojie are jointly responsible for signing the contract. Minister Zhu has telegraphed Chen, instructing him to come to Beijing to explain the reasons. Chen has gone to Hong Kong, which shows his guilt. Li Guojie is under surveillance in Shanghai and has considerable freedom. Because the circumstances of this case are significant, it is necessary to investigate the inside story. If Mr. Li has no ambiguous behavior, would the government investigate an innocent person? As for the rumor that 700,000 has already been paid for the loan, the American merchants have not announced it. It will be checked by the Board of Directors when they audit the accounts. If it is true, it will be refunded in full.

Urging Chen Fumu to Come to Beijing (Beijing Telegraph): After the Ministry of Transportation publishes the share registration method for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, it will immediately telegraph Liu Hongsheng, General Manager of the company, to establish a share registration office immediately. The registration office will publish a notice in the newspaper, informing all shareholders to come to the office to complete the registration in accordance with the regulations. Zhu Jiaju will also go to Shanghai on the 17th to explain various points to the American-owned China Trading Company and discuss with Song Ziwen, as well as with the General Manager, directors, and supervisors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, to prepare cash for the recovery of shares and other matters. Because the contract for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's property mortgage case was jointly signed by Chen Fumu and Li Guojie, Zhu Jiaju telegraphed Chen, instructing him to come to Beijing to answer questions. Chen telegraphed Zhu from Hong Kong on the 17th, only stating that there was nothing illegal about the contracts, and did not mention when he would come to Beijing. Li and Chen are the main persons responsible for signing the contract and cannot evade responsibility. Another telegram has been sent urging him to come quickly.

The Property Affairs Department Has Taken Over: General Manager Liu Hongsheng appointed Cai Lisheng as the director of the Property Affairs Department the day before yesterday. Director Cai went to take over at 1:00 PM, and the former director, Cheng Zhiyuan, handled the handover. Office operations resumed as usual yesterday.

Local News 2

Patrolman Injured, Rickshaw Driver Dies, Young Hostage Unharmed 182

Gun battle with bandits on Jiangwan Road

Bandits fled in disarray after over ten minutes

Weng Kelong recounts his ordeal

Remarkably articulate and poised

Yesterday afternoon, a kidnapping case occurred at the intersection of Qiwu Pu Road and Pingliang Road in Yangshupu. It was solved at the intersection of Xiangyin Road and Tiyu Hui Road in Jiangwan. Police and bandits exchanged more than 20 shots, injuring a patrolman. The hostage was rescued on the spot. The details of the investigation are described below:

One Person Got in the Car Midway: At 5:45 PM yesterday afternoon, two people suddenly arrived at the Donghai Motor Company on the west side of Daliang Wan Road, Pingliang Road. One of them, dressed in a gray cloth jacket and trousers and claiming to be Zhao Fulin, hired a car. The company assigned car number 17564 from the Concession and number 4420 from the Public Works Bureau to him, driven by the newly hired rickshaw driver Shen Xitang. They stated that they were going to the intersection of Longjiang Road and Qiwu Pu Road in Yangshupu. Halfway there, another person wearing a blue cloth jacket and trousers got into the car. When they reached Qiwu Pu Road, the three of them got out of the car together and told the rickshaw driver to drive the car to the intersection of Longjiang Road and wait for them. They then walked to the entrance of number 366, as if waiting for something.

Young Child Suddenly Snatched Away: Not long after, a young child walked out of number 366 and looked around outside the gate. At this time, the three bandits pulled out their pistols, stepped forward to scare the child into silence, and the one dressed in gray cloth jacket and trousers picked him up and put him in the car, threatening the rickshaw driver to drive quickly towards Jungong Road. At this time, the child's family had not yet found out. Later, after being told by neighbors, they urgently dispatched servants to search in all directions, but to no avail. They immediately went to the Yulin Road police station to report. The police station dispatched a large number of detectives by car to pursue them. After learning that the car had escaped in the direction of Jungong Road, they immediately notified the Municipal Public Security Bureau, which instructed the police stations in the five districts to pay attention through the Inspectorate.

Patrolman and Rickshaw Driver Injured: At around 7:30 PM, police officers from the Fifth Precinct, Fifth Sub-precinct police station in Jiangwan Tiyu Hui Road were inspecting pedestrians when a white-license taxi drove towards the intersection of Gongwan Road and Tiyu Hui Road on Xiangyin Road. The police officers stopped it for questioning as usual. Unexpectedly, the car suddenly fired two shots at the police officers. The police officers quickly returned fire, and the two sides engaged in a fierce battle for about ten minutes. The occupants of the car ran out of bullets and took advantage of the chaos to get out of the car and escape east on Tiyu Hui Road. The police officers immediately chased after them bravely, but the area was remote, sparsely populated, and it was dark, so the bandits escaped. They returned to the original location and saw that Police Sergeant Liu Feizhi had been shot and was bleeding profusely. They quickly helped him into the station. Upon inspection of the car, they saw that the rickshaw driver had also been injured, so they pulled him out of the car and carried him into the station.

Young Hostage Unharmed: When Police Officers Jing Lun, Wu Wenxiang, Wang Xianming, and Guo Qingyun returned to the police station, they saw that a young child and a public bus driver were already in the station. After questioning, they learned that the young child was the hostage in the car. After the kidnappers got out of the car and fled, the child also got out of the car and ran wildly towards Jiangwan Road. Seeing a China Merchants First Road public bus coming towards him, he shouted for it to stop. The bus driver immediately stopped and asked for the reason. The child told him about his encounter with the kidnappers. The driver then took him back to the police station to report and asked for protection, thus clarifying the case.

Rickshaw Driver Dies from Severe Injuries: At this time, Dai Hongen, Chief of the Fifth Precinct, Fifth Sub-precinct, had arrived with a large number of armed police officers. After learning that the kidnappers had escaped east on Tiyu Hui Road, he urgently telephoned the neighboring precinct stations, instructing the officers on duty to pay attention, and also reported the progress of the case to the head office. He immediately sent the injured rickshaw driver Shen Xitang and the Police Sergeant Liu Feizhi, who was injured in the line of duty, to the Tongren Hospital for treatment. It was found that the rickshaw driver had been shot in the left chest, with the bullet exiting from his back. Due to excessive blood loss, he died before he could be treated. The hospital reported it to the police station, which sent it to the morgue for examination. Police Sergeant Liu was shot in the right shoulder, the bullet exiting, and he was not seriously injured and is still receiving treatment.

Young Child Details the Ordeal: After the reporter learned that the Fifth Sub-precinct had solved the case, he rushed to investigate. First, he went to the police station, where he saw a car parked at the intersection of Xiangyin Road and Tiyu Hui Road, with shards of glass all over the ground. There was a pool of blood on the seat in the driver's seat. There was a hole in the wall under the door of the police station, shot by the kidnappers. There was no other damage. He then learned that the hostage had been sent to the sub-precinct, so he went to the sub-precinct. On the way, he met Chief Dai escorting the hostage to his home to notify them and prevent them from being anxious. The reporter asked the child about his kidnapping experience by the side of the car, as described above. He also learned that the child's name was Weng Kelong, eleven years old, from Chaozhou. His father's name was Jingqing, and he ran several pawnshops and clothing stores in Shanghai. He was studying at the Shihua School. Last night, when he was having dinner, he saw a car parked at the door, thinking that a guest had arrived, so he went out to greet them. Unexpectedly, three men next to him picked him up and put him in the car. The bandits ordered the rickshaw driver to go to Jungong Road first, then ordered him to turn to Zhongshan Road. When crossing the new Zhongshan Road Bridge, another person wearing a blue cloth jacket and trousers got into the car and proceeded towards Xiangyin Road. When approaching the intersection of Tiyu Hui Road, when the police officers ordered the car to stop, the car stopped and the bandits ordered the rickshaw driver to drive quickly. The rickshaw driver ignored them. The bandits were in a hurry and opened fire. He (the child referred to himself) saw the bandits get out of the car and escape, so he got out of the car and called for help. The child stated that he saw a China Merchants First Road public bus coming towards him, so he shouted for it to stop. The bus driver immediately stopped and asked for the reason. The child told him about his encounter with the kidnappers. The driver then took him back to the police station to report and asked for protection. The child's articulation was exceptionally clear, and his attitude was calm. He was truly rare. The child is currently still in the Fifth Sub-precinct and will be sent to the head office today. After completing the procedures, he will be returned to his family.

A Great Tragedy: Fire in Taiyuan Lane, Zhabei 183

About Ten Men, Women, and Children Burned to Death

A total of twelve charred bodies have been recovered yesterday.

At 5:10 AM yesterday morning, a fire broke out in the home of Shen Yuanxiang, who ran the Shen Rongji bookbinding shop, at number 34, Alley 3, Taiyuan Lane, Zhongxing Road, Zhabei. It destroyed a total of eight rooms in shikumen houses from number 33 to number 38, as well as one overhead building. Two of the houses were double-fronted. More than ten men, women, and children were burned to death. Twelve bodies were recovered yesterday. The details are described below:

The Rumor of the Fire: There are more than 70 houses in the area, which are owned by the Li family. They face south and back onto Zhongxing Road, with a large open space in the back. Most of the houses inside are rented to Anhui people who run weaving factories. Shen's house is in the last row in the middle. At about 5:00 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the attic on the second floor of the house. There were as many as nine shop assistants living in the attic. According to an apprentice, the fire was caused by a shop assistant smoking and accidentally throwing the cigarette butt into a pile of paper. According to Zhu Xingsheng, a tenant living in the pavilion room of the house, the fire was caused by a kerosene lamp being knocked over in the second-floor attic.

The Course of the Fire: After the fire broke out, the northwest wind was very strong, and the neighbors were all asleep. Although Shen's shop assistants shouted loudly, they were unable to escape in time. Therefore, most of them were buried in the fire. Because none of the deceased have been claimed by their families, it is impossible to investigate their names, and even the exact number of dead and injured is unknown. However, the local headman, Wang Shaoting, sent people to collect the charred bodies all day yesterday. By the evening, a total of eleven charred bodies of men, women, and children had been collected. None of their limbs were intact. Some had intestines protruding, some had their skulls broken open, some were covered in blood, and some had no heads at all. The various tragic scenes were unbearable to witness. It was later learned that there were three children and nine adults, seven women and two men, among them. Gu, the wife of Zhu Xingsheng, a tenant in Shen's pavilion room, was 49 years old and from Suzhou. Shen's wife, Luo, was 37 years old, and her son, Wan Shun, was only ten years old. Also, the Li family of five, two men and three women, living in the three-story attic in the back, and the Wan couple, Anhui natives, who lived there as well, were all burned to death. The bodies were all placed in the open air. The local headman was busy examining the charred bodies yesterday and had not yet requested an examination. He will report to the Shanghai District Court today to request an autopsy. Shen Yuanxiang, 45 years old, from Zhenjiang, has been taken into custody by the Fourth Precinct Public Security Bureau pending investigation. According to an investigation by the Taiyang Temple Police Station of the Fourth Precinct Public Security Bureau, the property losses of the affected households were approximately 15,400 yuan, and the property losses were also over 15,000 yuan.

The Beixin Bookstore Case Was Heard Yesterday 184

The Police Have Not Yet Decided Whether to Prosecute

According to the China Press, the Central Executive Yuan resolved to investigate the Beixin Bookstore in Shanghai for publishing words that insulted Islam. It has been heard that the Chinese authorities in Shanghai have discussed this matter with the Municipal Council because the Beixin Bookstore is located in the Concession. The First Special District Court sent an official document to the Police Department of the Municipal Council, requesting an investigation into the book. If the content is indeed contrary to the principle of freedom of belief, then the manager of the bookstore should be prosecuted. According to a certain police lawyer, although the Executive Yuan has issued an order to seal up the Beixin Bookstore, the official document from the First Special District Court did not ask the police to close the bookstore. As for whether the police should file a public prosecution against the bookstore, no decision has been made yet.

Lu Feibo Corrects His Remarks: The Shanghai Booksellers Association sent a letter to this newspaper regarding the Beixin Bookstore case. The reports in various newspapers in recent days have been quite inconsistent. Yesterday's Shenbao published Lu Feibo's remarks on the Beixin Bookstore case, which were based on an interview with a friend from a newspaper. However, the tone of what he recorded was slightly inaccurate. The corrections are as follows: (The other day, my old friend Mr. Huang told me that the Islamic leaders on Six Roads were powerful figures in various religions, so I sent a letter to arrange a meeting. Yesterday afternoon, I went to meet Chief Imam Ha Decheng. Chief Imam Ha said that this matter was not the concern of one mosque, but was presided over by the United Islamic Association. I said that I would send a letter to the association. At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, Chief Imam Ha sent a letter, instructing me not to send the letter. (The real situation of this first paragraph is that this was a private action and should not be published.) Some unscrupulous elements in the book industry publish books that are unsightly or print book samples and mail them to the interior. People in the interior send money to order, but often do not receive the books and often send letters to the Booksellers Association to inquire. When people are sent to investigate, there is no such store at the address. Therefore, the association recently published advertisements in various newspapers, instructing readers in the interior to inquire with the Booksellers Association if they have any doubts. (The fact in this second paragraph is a general discussion of the book industry situation. The Islamic community believes that the cartoon "Little Pig Eight Commandments" of the Beixin Bookstore is insulting. The book industry also expresses concern. Therefore, the Beixin Bookstore initially reported to the association, but the association did nothing, believing that under the rule of law, there should be a legal system to determine any guilt. Later, seeing the Executive Yuan's instructions, the book industry said that ordering the closure of the bookstore by administrative fiat rather than the law would put everyone in danger. On the one hand, the government should withdraw its order; on the other hand, it should present its case to the mayor and the government. But I felt that this matter would put both sides in a confrontational position, which would not be beneficial to anyone. Therefore, I ordered Beixin to send the book to the municipal government and apologize in the newspaper. On the one hand, I planned to ask the Islamic community to withdraw the request for a ban, seeking legal remedies instead. This would show the Islamic community's spirit of forgiveness and could save the government from sacrificing the rule of law. However, there are many mosques in Shanghai, and I did not know where to contact them, so I published my opinions in the newspaper, so that everyone could discuss the matter. The members of the association only seek to handle the matter according to the law and have no intention of supporting Beixin. This is the fact in the third paragraph.) The rumor that the police refused to enforce the ban was seen in the newspaper. The Booksellers Association did not participate. The rumor that the book industry went on strike to protest was also only seen in the newspaper. The Booksellers Association also did not know about it. (This last paragraph is the fact. I was seriously ill in the summer, and slightly better in the fall. I went to Tangshan for more than ten days to recuperate, and my health improved greatly. In recent days, my insomnia and diarrhea have returned. The doctor has ordered me to go out and rest. I will be leaving soon, and I will not be responsible for any reports in the newspapers in the future.]

Donations to the Northeast Volunteer Army - Yesterday's News 185

The Shanghai Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association, after many days of preparation for a fundraising event, has formally scheduled it for the 20th (Sunday) and 21st (Monday) of this month, to be held at the Tianchan Stage. Yesterday, theater tickets were sent to various sectors. A summary of letters and donations received by the association from various parties is recorded below:

Regarding the Sending of Tickets: All directors, executive members, and custody committee members, as well as inspection committee members, a total of sixty-eight individuals, jointly signed and sent letters to various sectors with enclosed theater tickets. The letter stated: "Respectfully, since the brutal Japanese army occupied Shenyang and completely removed the defenses of Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Northern China, and the battle in Liaodong is in full swing, our patriotic warriors, holding weapons, build their homes, and are now enduring the ice and snow, dodging bullets under the forests, fighting the enemy empty-handed, and serving in the army with empty stomachs. How can we not be saddened and shed tears? We are fortunate to be in the safety of a paradise, but we empathize with the suffering of the soldiers. Lone armies are far away, traveling thousands of miles listening to the sound of battle drums. The troops have no supplies of food or clothing. The borderland is bitterly cold, and we plan to provide relief from behind. Ashamed of our limited abilities, we have consulted celebrities and amateur performers, noble members, to perform Peking Opera for two days at Tianchan Stage. Borrowing the costumes of actors, we break the illusion of puppets, not relying on sensual allure, appearing on stage, vowing to risk our ardent blood sincerity to eliminate the ominous signs. We hope that you, esteemed Gongjin (referring to someone with great understanding), know the music, or ladies, or business giants, instead of throwing money at empty courtesans, indulging in mere entertainment, why not donate to the volunteer army and enjoy the pleasure of watching the show? Drive from afar, come together, accumulate like tributaries, collect a thousand fox furs, and add a spoonful to the pot. Inspire patriotic feelings, hope for the example of sacrificing one's family. Not only will the Ling and Luo mules from Zhenshan comfort the Western soldiers, but the soldiers will also be fed and emboldened to strip the souls of the Eastern barbarians."

The representative will go north within a week, and the affairs in Shanghai will be handled by staff member Cao Fengchun.

However, the representatives of the armies arriving in Shanghai lack organization, causing various difficulties. We hope for your assistance to help us achieve our goals. We are very fortunate."
